Let me understand the timeline:\n\n1. The backlight detection happens early in the boot process\n2. At that time, the intel_backlight device might not be registered yet\n3. So backlight_device_get_by_type(BACKLIGHT_RAW) returns NULL\n4. The system falls back to acpi_backlight_video\n5. The acpi_video backlight doesn't work on this hardware\n\nThen later, when intel_backlight is registered, it's too late for the backlight_notify callback to be meaningful, and the system has already set up the wrong backlight interface.\n\nWait, let me re-read the backlight_notify code...\n\nLooking at lines 380-397 in video_detect.c:\n```c\nstatic void acpi_video_backlight_notify_work(struct work_struct *work)\n{\n    if (acpi_video_get_backlight_type() != acpi_backlight_video)\n        acpi_video_unregister_backlight();\n}\n\nstatic int acpi_video_backlight_notify(struct notifier_block *nb,\n                       unsigned long val, void *bd)\n{\n    struct backlight_device *backlight = bd;\n    /* A raw bl registering may change video -> native */\n    if (backlight->props.type == BACKLIGHT_RAW &&\n        val == BACKLIGHT_REGISTERED)\n        schedule_work(&backlight_notify_work);\n\n    return NOTIFY_OK;\n}\n```\n\nThis callback is supposed to unregister the acpi_video backlight when a BACKLIGHT_RAW device is registered. However, it only unregisters if `acpi_video_get_backlight_type() != acpi_backlight_video`. The problem is that when the notify callback runs, it checks the current backlight type, but that type was already determined during boot when the raw device didn't exist yet. So the callback sees that the type is still acpi_backlight_video and doesn't unregister anything, even though a raw device is now available. get_backlight_type() is called in the notify handler and now detects the BACKLIGHT_RAW device, returning acpi_backlight_native instead of acpi_backlight_video. The condition checking if the type isn't acpi_backlight_video evaluates to true, triggering the unregister call. But that should actually work correctly.\n\nThe real issue might be different. When a BACKLIGHT_RAW device is registered (intel_backlight), the callback should:\n\n1. But there's a potential timing issue: if intel_backlight registers before the backlight_notifier callback is set up, the notification never fires and acpi_video stays registered.\n\nLooking at the initialization sequence, the notifier gets registered during the first call to acpi_video_get_backlight_type(). If intel_backlight loads before that happens, it won't trigger the unregistration. The problematic order would be: intel_backlight device registers, then later acpi_video_get_backlight_type() is called and sets up the notifier, but by then the intel_backlight event has already passed.\n\nThe core issue is that backlight_device_get_by_type(BACKLIGHT_RAW) finds the intel_backlight device, yet acpi_osi_is_win8() returns false, so the code still registers acpi_video instead. Since the notifier was registered after intel_backlight already loaded, it never catches the event to switch to native backlight. The solution involves either checking for BACKLIGHT_RAW existence before evaluating Win8 status to prioritize native backlight when available, or applying a DMI quirk for systems with this specific behavior. At line 1860-1861:\n```c\nif (acpi_video_get_backlight_type() != acpi_backlight_video)\n    return 0;\n```\n\nThis means that if the backlight type is NOT acpi_backlight_video (e.g., it's acpi_backlight_native or acpi_backlight_vendor), then acpi_video won't register its backlight interface.\n\nSo the problem is:\n1. During boot, acpi_video_get_backlight_type() is called\n2. At that time, the system might not be reporting as Win8\n3. So it returns acpi_backlight_video\n4. acpi_video registers its backlight interface\n5. Later, intel_backlight is registered (BACKLIGHT_RAW)\n6. But by then, acpi_video backlight is already registered and trying to control the brightness, which doesn't work\n\nThe fix should ensure that the system prefers native backlight even on non-Win8 systems if intel_backlight is available.\n\nHowever, looking at the code flow more carefully:\n\n1. First call to acpi_video_get_backlight_type() happens during ACPI video bus initialization\n2. At that point, the notifier is registered and init_work is set up\n3. When intel_backlight is registered, the backlight_notifier_block callback is triggered\n4. The callback schedules acpi_video_backlight_notify_work\n5. This work calls acpi_video_get_backlight_type() again\n6. Now, backlight_device_get_by_type(BACKLIGHT_RAW) should find intel_backlight\n7. But acpi_osi_is_win8() is still false\n8. So it still returns acpi_backlight_video\n9. And the callback condition `if (acpi_video_get_backlight_type() != acpi_backlight_video)` is false\n\n\n10. So acpi_video_unregister_backlight() is NOT called\n\nThe core issue is that when BACKLIGHT_RAW becomes available, the callback doesn't unregister acpi_video's backlight even though a native driver is now present. The solution could be to either modify the callback to unregister when native hardware is detected, or change acpi_video_get_backlight_type() to prioritize BACKLIGHT_RAW availability over the Win8 check, since the comment suggests this ordering was chosen to avoid behavior changes.\n\nReconsidering the sequence: acpi_video gets registered first and claims the backlight, then intel_backlight (BACKLIGHT_RAW) registers later. The notifier callback should handle this transition by unregistering acpi_video when a native driver appears, but it's not doing so because the Win8 condition prevents it from returning acpi_backlight_video. The intel_backlight device registers after acpi_video_bus_register_backlight() completes, so the initial type check returns acpi_backlight_video since BACKLIGHT_RAW doesn't exist yet.\n\nWhen intel_backlight finally registers, the notifier fires and calls acpi_video_get_backlight_type() again—this time BACKLIGHT_RAW is available, so it should return acpi_backlight_native. However, acpi_osi_is_win8() returns false on this system, so the function still returns acpi_backlight_video instead. The unregister condition then evaluates to false, leaving both drivers active and causing the brightness conflict.\n\nA DMI quirk for this specific model would work, though a more robust solution would be to remove the Win8 requirement or reorder the logic to prioritize BACKLIGHT_RAW detection. The callback logic attempts to unregister acpi_video when a different backlight type becomes available, but it only triggers on win8 systems. This means on older systems, even when native backlight (intel_backlight) registers, the acpi_video driver doesn't get unloaded as it should.\n\nThe core issue is in video_detect.c line 446, which gates the preference for BACKLIGHT_RAW behind an acpi_osi_is_win8() check. Removing this condition would make native backlight always take priority over ACPI video backlight, which is the correct behavior since hardware control is superior. However, that's a broader behavioral change that could affect other systems.\n\nFor the Acer TravelMate 5735Z specifically, the safest approach is adding a DMI quirk entry in video_detect.c to force native backlight on that model, following the existing pattern for other problematic My fault localization result is properly formatted and saved. Let me summarize what I found:\n\n## Summary of Findings\n\n### Bug Report Analysis\n- **System**: Acer TravelMate 5735Z with Intel GM45/GMA 4500MHD (2011 model)\n- **Issue**: ACPI video backlight brightness control doesn't work by default, but works with `acpi_backlight=native`\n- **Kernel Version**: Linux 5.6.7\n\n### Root Cause\nThe bug is in the backlight type detection logic in `drivers/acpi/video_detect.c`, specifically in the `acpi_video_get_backlight_type()` function at lines 446-447.\n\n### The Problem\nThe condition:\n```c\nif (acpi_osi_is_win8() && backlight_device_get_by_type(BACKLIGHT_RAW))\n    return acpi_backlight_native;\n```\n\nThis requires BOTH conditions to be true:\n1. System reports as Windows 8 compatible\n2. A BACKLIGHT_RAW device (intel_backlight) is available\n\nFor the Acer TravelMate 5735Z:\n- It has a working intel_backlight device (BACKLIGHT_RAW)\n- But it doesn't report as Win8-compatible (BIOS from 2011)\n- Therefore, the function falls back to `acpi_backlight_video`\n- But ACPI video backlight control doesn't work on this hardware\n\n### Impact\nWhen ACPI video backlight is selected, it tries to control brightness through ACPI methods that don't work on this hardware.
